  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

  <span id="freeText10767989416235873" style="display:none"><b>A heartbroken girl. A fierce warrior. A hero in the making.</b><br /><br />Sixteen years ago the Kingdom of Winter was conquered and its citizens enslaved, leaving them without magic or a monarch. Now, the Winterians’ only hope for freedom is the eight survivors who managed to escape, and who have been waiting for the opportunity to steal back Winter’s magic and rebuild the kingdom ever since.<br /><br />Orphaned as an infant during Winter’s defeat, Meira has lived her whole life as a refugee, raised by the Winterians’ general, Sir. Training to be a warrior—and desperately in love with her best friend, and future king, Mather — she would do anything to help her kingdom rise to power again.<br /><br />So when scouts discover the location of the ancient locket that can restore Winter’s magic, Meira decides to go after it herself. Finally, she’s scaling towers, fighting enemy soldiers, just as she’s always dreamed she would. But the mission doesn’t go as planned, and Meira soon finds herself thrust into a world of evil magic and dangerous politics – and ultimately comes to realize that her destiny is not, never has been, her own.</span>

//<![CDATA[
  var timer_310073_end_at = 1849133 + new Date().getTime()/1000;

  function timer_310073_updateTimer() {
    var time_left = "";
    var secs_left = timer_310073_end_at - new Date().getTime()/1000;

    if(secs_left <= 0) {
      document.getElementById("timer_310073").innerHTML = "closed";
      clearInterval(timer_310073_updater);
      return;
    }

    var minutes_left = secs_left / 60;
    var hours_left = minutes_left / 60;
    var days_left = Math.floor(hours_left / 24);

    if(days_left > 0) {
      if(false){
        time_left += days_left + ":";
      }else{
        time_left += days_left + " days and ";
      }
    }
    if(false){
      time_left += Math.floor(hours_left%24/10)
      time_left += Math.floor(hours_left%24)%10 + ":";
    }else{
      time_left += Math.floor(hours_left%24) + ":";
    }
    time_left += Math.floor(minutes_left%60/10);
    time_left += Math.floor(minutes_left%10) + ":";
    time_left += Math.floor(secs_left%60/10);
    time_left += Math.floor(secs_left%10);

    document.getElementById("timer_310073").innerHTML = time_left;
  }

  timer_310073_updateTimer();
  var timer_310073_updater = setInterval(timer_310073_updateTimer, 100);
//]]>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is romance, I guess, but not really. The story isn't about the romance... it's about the restoration of a king to his throne. I would give it a <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is romance, I guess, but not really. The story isn't about the romance... it's about the restoration of a king to his throne. I would give it a 4 in romance just because it IS there, and there is a small story line about love and duty, but it isn't the main thing. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_854442039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/854442039" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/854442039?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer854442039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5419185636667223644"><blockquote>
  <i>I wanted to be a soldier. Someone who would earn standing in Winter. Someone Sir would look at with pride. Someone Mather would look at and—<br/><br/>No.</i>
</blockquote>This is one of the best high fantasy I've read this year, which might not mean much, considering the crap I've read, but I can only attest to my enjoyment of it. This book is good. <br/><br/>But...but<b> there's the love triangle.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I’m at the center of this, a weird possessive feud between the Winter king and the Cordellan prince.</i>
</blockquote><b>Why there gotta be a love triang</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5419185636667223644" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I wanted to be a soldier. Someone who would earn standing in Winter. Someone Sir would look at with pride. Someone Mather would look at and—<br /><br />No.</i>
</blockquote>This is one of the best high fantasy I've read this year, which might not mean much, considering the crap I've read, but I can only attest to my enjoyment of it. This book is good. <br /><br />But...but<b> there's the love triangle.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I’m at the center of this, a weird possessive feud between the Winter king and the Cordellan prince.</i>
</blockquote><b>Why there gotta be a love triangle, man?!</b> For all that's holy...<br /><br />But onto the good. This book has:<br /><br />1. A well-developed <b>setting</b> and an <b>engrossing story</b>, those of you who've read <i>Game of Thrones</i> will find the season-based setting in this book very, very familiar<br /><br />2. A <b>strong female main character</b> who will not make your head hurt, and <b>complex relationships</b> between side characters<br /><br />3. A believable romance. Fine, there is a fucking love triangle that is truly, truly stretched out. The good thing is that <b>both love interests are deeply likeable</b><br /><br />...which just ends up making it more painful WHEN YOU LIKE BOTH GUYS. ARG!<br /><br />By the way, this is <b>a fucking long book</b>. Seriously fucking long. It could stand to be cut 50 pages.<br /><br /><u>The Summary</u>:<blockquote>
  <i>I’m running. Running through gray streets choked with smoke as hordes of people run too, more explosions corralling us into Angra’s grasp. That’s what they’re doing—corralling the Winterians like sheep so they can lead them to a life of slavery and pain.<br /><br />Except for us. The seven who still live with Winter’s future king. Originally twenty-five refugees who kept Angra up at night, reduced to eight.</i>
</blockquote>Young <b>Meira</b>'s life is dire. She is an orphan, but she's not the only one. She's lucky to be an orphan, because that means at least she, out of her family, has survived.<br /><br />The kingdom of Winter lies in ruins. Destroyed by an evil magician, a psychopath. Hundreds of thousands of Winterians are dead. God knows how many are left...but for Meira, her world consists of her little army of 8. The rest are dead, disappeared, gone. Within the eight survivors are <b>"Sir"</b>, the hardened soldier who rescued young Meira when she was but a child, and <b>Mather</b>...Winter's future king.<br /><br />King in name only, that is, because there is no Winter to return to.<br /><br />Mather and Meira are friends, fellow fighters. She is a soldier, and so is he. They have been trained to fight and survive. Sparks fly between them, but there can never be a future for the two of them, during peace or war.<blockquote>
  <i>No matter our dire circumstances, no matter our shared upbringing, no matter the chill his smile sends over my body, he’s still him, and I’m still me, and yes, he needs to have a female heir someday, but with a proper lady, a duchess or a princess—not the girl who spars with him.</i>
</blockquote>The problem lies <b>beyond Winter's destruction.</b> It lies in the fact that <b>Mather, the heir to Winter, is a male</b>. The kingdom of Winter is <b>a matriarchy</b>, where magic is passed on through a <b>female-blooded conduit.</b> As a male, Mather is nigh useless. Except as <b>a breeding stud for a future queen.</b><br /><br />(That's quite a nice change!)<br /><br />There's also the fact that the magical Conduit is missing. Stolen. Hidden. In two pieces, and useless until they can be reunited.<br /><br />There's also the fact that The Decay rips across the land, destroying it. Sneaking into people's hearts. Making them do horrible things.<br /><br />There's also the fact that the evil tyrant still remains, his goal to destroy the kingdoms. To wipe Winter---and its heir, out of existence.<br /><br />From all this mess, what can one girl do? <b>Meira has no magic. She is not the strongest fighter.</b> All she has is <b>strength, determination, willpower, and an immense sense of loyalty to her kingdom.</b><br /><br />Is that enough? Will Meira be content to be a pawn?<blockquote>
  <i>You don’t know anything, Meira, and I’m sorry if this...is hard for you to accept, but it will happen. You wanted to matter to Winter? This is how Winter needs you.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Or will Meira become the person she knew she could be all along?</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Don’t you want more than this?” I breathe.<br /><br />“Every day of my life.”</i>
</blockquote><u>The Setting</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>It’s so cold that foreigners have to wrap in layers of fur to walk from building to building, while our natural Winterian blood keeps us warm even in the worst conditions. And snow is everywhere, always, so much that the grass beneath it is white from lack of sun. An entire kingdom wrapped in an orb of eternal winter.</i>
</blockquote>Call it a GoT clone if you want, but I quite loved the setting in this book. There are the <b>Rhythm kingdoms</b>...countries with seasons, and the <b>Season kingdoms</b>...countries with just one season each. Spring. Summer. Fall. Winter. Each with their own characteristics. Each with their own eternal seasons. Each with their distinguishing features within their people.<br /><br />The Winter kingdom, for instance...obviously remain in <b>perpetual winter.</b> And the strength of their people reflect their harsh conditions. They cannot imagine a life without endless cold, they think the people of the warmer climes are weaklings. Their coloring reflect their country. Winterians, for example, all have <b>snow-white skin and hair.</b><br /><br />The different kingdoms have their different customs---and curses. They think the others are barbaric and savages. I enjoyed everything about the world-building, the magic, and the setting within this book. <b>It was intricately built.</b><br /><br /><u>Meira</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>But no matter how dire our situation, how desperate Sir gets, he will never see me as an asset. Just the overexcited child he had the misfortune of raising.</i>
</blockquote><b>Meira is one of the strongest characters I've read in high fantasy this year.</b> Again, given the absolute crap I've read this year, that might not say much, but allow me to say that <b>there is nothing about her that I hated.</b><br /><br />She is a soldier, above all else. She can fight, and she fights---repeatedly, for her life.<blockquote>
  <i>I cannot die like Crystalla...I still have my knife. I still have a chance.</i>
</blockquote>Yes, Meira has <i>feeeeeeeeeelings</i>, but they feel normal, unobtrusive. A momentary spike of teenaged hormones instead of overwhelming insta-love or lust, or anything heaviliy romantic that persists throughout the book. Her feelings and her emotions are normal, and utterly relatable.<br /><br />Meira is strong, and stubborn, but never, ever TSTL (too-stupid-to-live). She is <b>never cut your nose to spite your face kind of dumb.</b> She doesn't like dresses. She likes being a tomboy, but when she has to wear one. Hey, why not. Enjoy the frill while it lasts. Don't fight it. It's for a good cause.<blockquote>
  <i>My hair, a giant array of pinned-back curls, hangs messy yet soft with a few white strands dangling free around my face.<br /><br />I click my mouth shut. Maybe being a little fancier isn’t a horrible thing.</i>
</blockquote>One of the things I loved most about Meira is <b>her relationship with her guardian, Sir.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Occasionally I could catch a flicker—a twinge around his eyes when Mather faltered in sparring, a twitch of his lips when I begged to learn how to fight. But that was all I ever saw of the general who once carried a baby for days to safety. Like all of his actual tenderness was gone, but every so often his muscles convulsed from the memory of it.</i>
</blockquote>I loved their complex relationship. I loved his harshness, and his unwincing criticism of her. I loved the way she constantly strives for, never quite reaching his approval. I loved his love for her, so obvious that anyone can see it but her. I love the way she constantly doubts herself, the way she constantly tries and tries and tries to <b>just be good enough in his eyes.</b> I love their love-hate relationship. It is one of the best relationships I've ever read in a high fantasy.<br /><br /><u>The Romance</u>: Really. Why there gotta be a love triangle, man?<b> Especially when one of the love interest is...this.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Thank you.” I nod to his ankle. “For everything. You didn’t—”<br />He shakes his head. “Yes, I did. You deserve to fight for your home as much as the rest of us do.”</i>
</blockquote>And this.<blockquote>
  <i>Mather never got mad at me for pulling him into mischief or for breaking during Sir’s interrogations. He’d just smile, throw his arm around me, and say something encouraging.<br />Mather has always been a king, every moment of his life.</i>
</blockquote>Really, I hated it. I loved Mather, despite his name, which always brings to mind Eminem (AKA Marshall Mathers of the I'm slim shady fame). Mather is such a good love interest, which made me root for him.<br /><br />WHICH MADE IT EVEN SUCKIER WHEN I COULDN'T EVEN HATE THE OTHER LOVE INTEREST. Who is not a king, but a prince. And man, is he a princely prince. He's not even a douchebag! He is a king, playful, gentlemanly prince who...CARES ABOUT HIS PEOPLE. How the fuck does a girl choose?!<blockquote>
  <i>He knows all of them. Every single one. And not only that, but he seems genuinely interested in them, remembering not only dozens of faces but also the smallest details about how that back acre of farmland is doing, did the trade with Yakim go well last week, is your daughter settled with her new husband yet?</i>
</blockquote><b>Why there gotta be a love triangle, man?</b><br /><br />The only reservations I have about this book is that I couldn't connect to the main character...she was fine. There was nothing wrong with her. I thoroughly liked her, but she was <b>missing a spark</b> that makes me truly love a character. Furthermore, it was <b>extremely predictable</b>. Seriously. <b>I guessed the twist</b> within 15% of the book.<br /><br />Overall, solid, solid buy. Read it.<br /><br /><i>All quotes were taken from an advanced copy subject to change in the final edition.</i></span>

<div id="review_856006950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/856006950" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/856006950?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer856006950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9392091576050914850"><blockquote>
  <i>No matter what happens, no matter who turns on me, no matter what pompous swine thinks he has power over me, I am still me. I will always be me.</i>
</blockquote><br/>3 1/2 stars. Okay, let's get some things straight first. <br/><br/><b>Q:</b> Will this book offer a never before seen plot with mind-blowing originality and absolutely definitely no love triangle? <br/><b>A:</b> Nuh-uh. <br/><br/><b>Q:</b> But did I get completely sucked into this world and ended up wildly entertained for the last few hours in which I read the book in a single sitting? <br/><b>A:</b> Hell y</span>
  <span id="freeText9392091576050914850" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>No matter what happens, no matter who turns on me, no matter what pompous swine thinks he has power over me, I am still me. I will always be me.</i>
</blockquote><br />3 1/2 stars. Okay, let's get some things straight first. <br /><br /><b>Q:</b> Will this book offer a never before seen plot with mind-blowing originality and absolutely definitely no love triangle? <br /><b>A:</b> Nuh-uh. <br /><br /><b>Q:</b> But did I get completely sucked into this world and ended up wildly entertained for the last few hours in which I read the book in a single sitting? <br /><b>A:</b> Hell yes!<br /><br />Anyone who's a fan of YA fantasy will recognise familiar elements of the genre in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17399160.Snow_Like_Ashes__Snow_Like_Ashes___1_" title="Snow Like Ashes (Snow Like Ashes, #1) by Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener">Snow Like Ashes</a>. A strong heroine, royal politics, reclaiming a stolen kingdom, a touch of magic and, yes, even a love triangle. But it is in the details of this story where the book finds its strength and still manages, in my opinion, to stand out from many of a similar ilk.<br /><br />For one thing, <b>I absolutely loved Meira</b>. She's as badass as Katsa from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3236307.Graceling__Graceling_Realm___1_" title="Graceling (Graceling Realm, #1) by Kristin Cashore" rel="nofollow noopener">Graceling</a> but without the troubling pseudo-feminist propaganda. From the very beginning, she wants to fight for the Winterians, she refuses to be beaten down by the expectations of others, but she is also a flawed, complex and sympathetic character.<br /><br />However, she doesn't hold up this novel alone. <b>ALL the characters are well-developed and the character dynamics are superb</b>. Raasch has built up an interesting and complicated web of relationships between them, their situation putting further strain on their ties to one another:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>That’s how we all are, too hard for what we should be. We should be a family, not soldiers. But all that really connects us is stories, and memories, of what should be.</i>
</blockquote><br />A love triangle typically has me rolling my eyes and yet here I liked both Mather and Theron. I can see how their differences could make it a genuinely difficult choice - should Meira be with the soldier she has loved all her life, or the poet willing to start a war for her? For once I find myself excited to see what will happen between them next.<br /><br />The book does get a touch info-dumpy in parts, but I was honestly thankful for the world-building. The author has crafted a fascinating setting of eight kingdoms, each with their own customs, ideals and magic. The history is woven in seamlessly, bringing this exciting and horrifying place to life in my mind.<br /><br /><b>And parts of this book are indeed horrifying</b>. Meira and her seven Winterian companions have had a hard life, running from those who want to destroy any chance of Winter's throne being reclaimed. I just couldn't put it down. Bloody action scenes give way to shocking betrayals give way to not-so-shocking twists (seriously, I guessed it way in advance, but whatever, it was still fun!).<br /><br />I feel like I shouldn't like this. Like I should be pointing out that stupid love triangle and the same old tropes, instead of wondering who Meira will end up with and whether to drop my other books and read the sequel... <b>but damn - what can I say? - it was just crazy entertaining.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCcVsMUSAzMlIKs3nw-xe_nw" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9392091576050914850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1192828716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192828716" />
    <a title="Sasha Alsberg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10915830-sasha-alsberg"><img alt="Sasha Alsberg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512748008p2/10915830.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192828716?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_852889116" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852889116" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/852889116?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People new to high fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=can-t-believe-i-finished">can-t-believe-i-finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=print-arc">print-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=bea-2014">bea-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=cool-author">cool-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer852889116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2454002159024266108">I tried really hard to like <em>Snow Like Ashes</em>. Really hard. There are a lot of things a person might try to do. You can <em>try</em> to ride a bike. <em>Try</em> to draw. <em>Try</em> to, I don't know, jump off a cliff. And that's when I realized I was being completely ridiculous. You can't force yourself to like something no matter how hard you try. So I stopped trying and just continued reading, mostly because I really hate DNFing books, and took the pressure off of myself. Needless to day, <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> never improved </span>
  <span id="freeText2454002159024266108" style="display:none">I tried really hard to like <em>Snow Like Ashes</em>. Really hard. There are a lot of things a person might try to do. You can <em>try</em> to ride a bike. <em>Try</em> to draw. <em>Try</em> to, I don't know, jump off a cliff. And that's when I realized I was being completely ridiculous. You can't force yourself to like something no matter how hard you try. So I stopped trying and just continued reading, mostly because I really hate DNFing books, and took the pressure off of myself. Needless to day, <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> never improved for me.<br><br><strong>Be warned that this review will be full of spoilers</strong>, but not really since you can figure everything out by the second chapter. But I thought I'd at least throw it out there.<br><br>The basic premise around <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> is one you've read before. There's a kingdom that has been ruined by an evil king of another kingdom, imprisoning its subjects and killing the queen. However, a few survive, including a knight, an heir to the throne, an orphaned girl and a bunch of other people who serve absolutely no other purpose other than existing. For 16 years, this group seeks a magic locket that will somehow help free their people and restore the magic of the Winter kingdom.<br><br>The story is told from Meira's point of view, a girl who was orphaned during collapse of Winter. She's just a normal girl trying to fit in and belong to the cause. A girl who prefers combat over dresses. <strong>Meira is <em>not</em> a terrible heroine, but one I had <em>zero</em> emotional connection with.</strong> If you are like me, you'll probably start wondering from chapter one why the author decided to tell this story from Meira's point of view. And by chapter two you'll notice a few things:<br><br>- Mather, the heir to the Winter throne, flinches when he is referred to as the king<br>- Sir told Meira from a young age not to call him "father"<br>- The magic of Winter is always passed down to a female<br>- Sir never lets Meira go on the dangerous missions, but somehow it's a great idea to send their heir, Mather...<br>- Mather feels bad that he won't be able to use Winter's magic even after they get the locket back<br><br>And if that's not enough to persuade you that something fishy is going on there are these clues by 40%:<br><br>- Of course Meira would be betrothed to a Prince and promised a title after Winter was restored<br>- The Cordellan king calls Mather <em>king</em> in italics<br>- Hannah, the dead Queen of Winter, appears in Meira's dreams all the time<br><br>Am I being subtle enough for you?<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Meira is the heir of Winter and she's one hell of a hipster princess. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Unfortunately for me, that killed most of the enjoyment I might have received from <em>Snow Like Ashes</em>. <strong>Knowing the big plot twist from the very beginning diminished my anticipation of getting to the end</strong> and having that "AH HA!" moment that I love so much in stories.<br><br>The world in <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> is a basic one. There are 8 kingdoms: 4 Seasons and 4 Rhythms, each with their own conduit filled with magic. Spring is ruled by Angra, a dominating and oppressive leader hell bent on destroying Winter. The reason why he's so focused isn't very clear and I'm thinking that might be part of the deeper plot of the trilogy. The issue I had is how the world is described to the reader. <strong>Info dumps plague <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> in the worst possible way.</strong> But then it's taken a step further with Meira giving explanations of the info dumps.<br><blockquote>Just as Winter focused its magic on mining, Coredell focuses its conduit on opportunity--on helping its citizenswork a situation in their favor so they get the most out of it. Opportunistic, resourceful, swindlers: whatever they're called, they can make "leaves turn to gold"--a Cordellan phrase Sir explained in our many lessons, referring to the fact that they're so good at turning a profit it's as if they make leaves on a tree turn into gold coins. That explains Captain Dominick's curse earlier--<em>golden leaves</em>.</blockquote><br>Maybe it's just me, but I didn't need this explanation and <strong>many times it felt like Meira over-monologued her monologues</strong> and talked her way into complete circles. This coupled with <strong>a plot that felt very contrived</strong>, especially in the beginning, didn't always make for an enjoyable reading experience for me.<br><br>- Meira is allowed to go on a really dangerous mission to collect half of the locket because Mather lies to Sir about her besting him in close range combat. A lie that was not at all convincible.<br>- This is Meira first dangerous mission and she just <em>happens</em> to overhear where the locket is located by people who were warned not to speak the location out loud.<br>- After 16 years of trying to get this half of the locket, Meira succeeds because this really dangerous villain put her on a horse, conveniently, without checking her first for weapons, and she gallops away.<br>- Shockingly, no one pursues her.<br><br>I just don't buy that. Just like I don't buy the names of the Seasons' capitols: Juli, Ocktuber, Jannuari and Abril. Sure these may seem like great obvious choices to play off months in which these seasons flourish if you live in the Northern Hemisphere of the world. But if you perhaps live in Australia or Asia, January is the exact opposite of winter... it's summer. It was little things like this that left <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> feeling very unpolished.<br><br>And now I feel bad because I haven't exactly said anything good about this book. But the thing is, nothing really sticks out for me. <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> failed to completely capture my interest and, therefore, is more of a meh read. One that isn't terrible, but that I won't remember much about to actually recommend it to someone.<br><br>But there was one scene that stuck out: the dick fight. Prince Theron and Mather just had to flex their muscles at each other over Meira. I understood Mather's reaction because he's in love with Meira and doesn't like the idea of her marrying Theron. But what about Theron? Pride maybe? Is he territorial? All I know is that, Mather started beating on his chest and Theron thought that was a great time to start comparing dick sizes.<br><blockquote>"No matter what I use, I always hit my mark."</blockquote><br>Things just start getting more and more ridiculous from there with Meira's monologuing.<br><blockquote>No man can refuse to answer that call.</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424564213i/13778207.jpg" alt=" photo bear fight_zpswwzk85bl.jpg" width="390" height="398" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>It's the kind of sword fight Sir has told stories about...</blockquote><br>Sir, has warned Meira of these Mythical Fights of the Dick.<br><br>Meanwhile, I was all...<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/sailor_stephie/status/568226170610819072">https://twitter.com/sailor_stephie/st...</a><br><br>So yup, that was the best part of the book and then it got boring again. I find out the big plot twist and discovered... oh wait... I already knew the plot twist and that made that little scene really anticlimactic. At that point, I was just waiting for the book to end. I had gotten that far and refused to give up because I'm really stubborn and I enjoy torturing myself. Though, in hindsight, I probably should have stopped.<br><br>Basically, this book just wasn't for me. That doesn't mean you shouldn't check it out, but if you <em>do</em> decide to give it a go and you aren't impressed by chapter 5, chances are it isn't for you either.<br><br>ARC was acquired at Book Expo America 2014. I was not paid for this review. <br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2454002159024266108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_855850520" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855850520" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855850520?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=war-setting">war-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855850520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17844366473104318921"><b>
  <blockquote>‘‘It’s too easy to throw balance into chaos.’’</blockquote>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413348810i/11499921._SY540_.jpg' width='430' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>This was an interesting, mostly positive, surprise. I did not know what I was getting into, perhaps, for there are many things I wasn’t expecting to discover.<br/><br/>While, overall, I found Meira to be a good fantasy heroine, there are some specific scenes, that could have been avoided or modifided, making her, somehow, get out of her character—a strong and fierce one. It is that she is quite reckless and there are moments when she can’t control her emo</span>
  <span id="freeText17844366473104318921" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>‘‘It’s too easy to throw balance into chaos.’’</blockquote>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413348810i/11499921._SY540_.jpg" width="430" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This was an interesting, mostly positive, surprise. I did not know what I was getting into, perhaps, for there are many things I wasn’t expecting to discover.<br><br>While, overall, I found Meira to be a good fantasy heroine, there are some specific scenes, that could have been avoided or modifided, making her, somehow, get out of her character—a strong and fierce one. It is that she is quite reckless and there are moments when she can’t control her emotions and acts. I did want her to be acting in a more mature way, during some scenes, because she can get childish at certain moments.<br><br>For example:<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>‘‘Meira, this isn’t going to fix anything—’’<br>‘‘Don’t care.’’<br>‘‘I’ve talked to him every day since he announced <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the engagement <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>; if I can’t change his mind—’’<br>I grit my teeth. ‘‘I. Don’t. Care.’’<br>
</blockquote>
</b><br>Why don’t you try listening to what he has to say, huh, Meira? Although, this was a little observation. She is still a kick-ass heroine.<br><br><u>There is a love-triangle</u>. I know I shouldn’t be surprised anymore—YA is filled with them—but it’s still disappointing, since I expected another kind of romance. Meira is in love with her childhood friend who has always taken care of her, Mather, but they can’t be together. He’s the next in line to become King of Winter and, well, she’s an orphan. But, then, circumstances are that she meets another prince, Theron. She may not have had the best of opinions on him at first but they slowly get to know each other and she even comes to like him…Well, that wasn’t hard to predict.<br><br>The pacing is very slow. I personally didn’t mind it at all because, since there is a war setting, it is very normal. This kind of plot needs slowness to plan and prepare and make us understand the context, so it definitely was alright for me. However, I did think that the plot focused too much on that. At first, I thought it wa going to be overwhelmed with romance, but I was very wrong. I did enjoy the story because of how invested I was. What happened to the Winter kingdom was very sad and unfair and I was agreeing with the Winterians doing whatever they could to get their magic back.<br><br>Characterization wasn’t missing in this book at all. They are, of course, some characters you will appreciate and others you will despise—that’s how much it can vary from one to another—but they certainly are well-developed and worth encountering. I personally really liked reading about Theron and how he started to stand up for what is important for him and the people. Incidentally, while I did like his character, I think it would be more interesting if he and Meira, in the sequels, stayed friends and build a strong boy/girl friendship because, effectively, those are possible.<br><br>The writing was one thing I liked most of this story. Well-written, in my opinion, as only a certain amount of fantasy authors that risk themselves in this impressive genre know how to write. The kind that will absorb you and won't let go of your interest, until you reach the last page.<br><br>If you find yourself in front of this book, don’t hesitate—it is worth it! I may only have rated it three stars, but I believe it is a good fantasy story that will only improve with its sequels, and I am looking forward to read them.<br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17844366473104318921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/999691526" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/999691526?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer999691526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12182035076465575038"><u>
  <b>Recycling My First Reviews: A Trip Down Memory Lane, Vol. 1</b>
</u><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Then</u>
</b> <br/>.<br/>.<br/><br/>Snow and ice and frost above, that was <b>ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I HAVE EVER READ</b>!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445894307ra/16714568.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can't believe it took me so long to start reading it! Everything, <i>everything</i> that makes fantasy my favorire genre was dominant in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17399160.Snow_Like_Ashes__Snow_Like_Ashes___1_' title='Snow Like Ashes (Snow Like Ashes, #1) by Sara Raasch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Snow Like Ashes</a>; the <b>unique world</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6947727.Sara_Raasch' title='Sara Raasch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sara Raasch</a> created, with the magic's source, the division of the nations based on the season/weather, the evil, <b>cruel monarch</b> who sought unlimited power without hesitating to meddle</span>
  <span id="freeText12182035076465575038" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Recycling My First Reviews: A Trip Down Memory Lane, Vol. 1</b>
</u><br><br><b>
  <u>Then</u>
</b> <br>.<br>.<br><br>Snow and ice and frost above, that was <b>ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I HAVE EVER READ</b>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445894307ra/16714568.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't believe it took me so long to start reading it! Everything, <i>everything</i> that makes fantasy my favorire genre was dominant in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17399160.Snow_Like_Ashes__Snow_Like_Ashes___1_" title="Snow Like Ashes (Snow Like Ashes, #1) by Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener">Snow Like Ashes</a>; the <b>unique world</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6947727.Sara_Raasch" title="Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener">Sara Raasch</a> created, with the magic's source, the division of the nations based on the season/weather, the evil, <b>cruel monarch</b> who sought unlimited power without hesitating to meddle with <b>dark forces</b>, the insane plot twists, the <b>battles</b> and, above all, a heroine who desperately wanted to find her place in the world without realizing that the fate of her nation depended on her.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Someday we will be more than words in the dark.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Meira was <b>hope</b>, the only hope of a doomed people, born in a sacked city, her roots cut off, her destiny unsure. The only certainty was that she wanted to <i>matter</i> to Winter, and Sir and Mather and everyone who seemed to think of her as a silly girl. That need made her reckless but she was definitely made of the hero material, I came to like her a lot! And of course, <b>I totally adored Theron</b>! He understood her, he wanted to fit in a world that was designed for him by others without losing his identity, he sook what was right, he was so noble and fair! And to my astonishment, I didn't mind the love triangle, perhaps because it wasn't in the spotlight and it lacked drama (praise the snow above)! I can't wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17404295.Ice_Like_Fire__Snow_Like_Ashes___2_" title="Ice Like Fire (Snow Like Ashes, #2) by Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener">Ice Like Fire</a>, next months will be insufferable! <b>A wonderful read, one I am thankful it came into my life!</b><br>.<br>.<br><br><b>
  <u>Now</u>
</b><br><br>I'm still in love with Theron (I guess some things never change). <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470169813ra/19897482.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have to give you a fair <b>
  <u>WARNING</u>
</b>, though: Do <b>NOT</b>, I repeat <b>DO NOT</b> read the second instalment, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17404295.Ice_Like_Fire__Snow_Like_Ashes___2_" title="Ice Like Fire (Snow Like Ashes, #2) by Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener">Ice Like Fire</a>. It will ruin you, and not in a good way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12182035076465575038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_853313677" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/853313677" />
    <a title="Naomi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1747782-naomi"><img alt="Naomi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310490815p2/1747782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/853313677?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi" href="/user/show/1747782-naomi">Naomi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer853313677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6946412796096177621">February 12, 2014: <br/>Am I the only one that notices that's Xena Warrior Princess's second Chakram on the front cover? I'm not joking.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392262081i/8528541._SX540_.jpg' width='280' height='380' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392262448i/8528635._SY540_.jpg' width='250' height='380' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Hmm, maybe I'll read this.<br/><br/>February 3, 2015:<br/><br/>Okay, so I've written and rewritten my review like a hundred times and I'm kind of sick and tired of writing it now. For now, this is how I feel about the book. This is edited out of 7 pages of half reviews, so don't expect it to be perfect by any means: <br/><br/>I finished Snow Like Ashes disappointed because I never felt that spark</span>
  <span id="freeText6946412796096177621" style="display:none">February 12, 2014: <br>Am I the only one that notices that's Xena Warrior Princess's second Chakram on the front cover? I'm not joking.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392262081i/8528541._SX540_.jpg" width="280" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392262448i/8528635._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hmm, maybe I'll read this.<br><br>February 3, 2015:<br><br>Okay, so I've written and rewritten my review like a hundred times and I'm kind of sick and tired of writing it now. For now, this is how I feel about the book. This is edited out of 7 pages of half reviews, so don't expect it to be perfect by any means: <br><br>I finished Snow Like Ashes disappointed because I never felt that spark. The spark that tells you you want to read more, you want to know what happens to these characters, and you want to really be a part of their world. The book is from Meira’s point of view, so I feel like I’m mainly missing her spark, something to pull her out and say I’m not just an average heroine.<br><br>Meira has her temper tantrums and whiney moments like other YA novels, but that’s not all there is to her and they’re fewer than most female leads I’ve seen in a while. Meira makes up for it enough for me by wielding a Chakram, actually fighting, and her sense of humor. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ “Congratulations, everyone. You’ve finally broken Meira, the crazy, orphaned soldier-girl. She’s snapped, all thanks to the mention of floral arrangements.” ~Meira  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Meira isn’t Xena by a long shot, but she’s still very likeable. She’s just missing that little spark that makes her something more. <br><br>Theron is my favorite character of this book. He’s just so selfless. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ When he sacrifices himself to force his father’s hand to help Meira, I fell in love with him. If Mather had come in, I feel like it wouldn’t have been as powerful.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He knows all his servants by name and also asks about how they’re truly doing. He spars with his soldiers and even created a map on their wall to remind them of who they are. Not to mention Theron is just really wise with all of his knowledge.<br><br>Mather is the second part of this love triangle. (I know, I hate love triangles too.) Mather isn’t a bad choice either for Meira, but I felt like Theron was just more developed than Mather. Mather kind of had a few moments where he was all jealous and very annoying. What’s worse, he put himself in that situation. There are a few moments that I really did like Mather, he has these really sweet and cute moments with Meira. At the end of the day, he’s going to have to prove it to me in the next book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Still kind of ticked that Mather knew Meira was the real princess and got mad at her for doing what she had to. Not to mention he knew about the arranged marriage and doesn’t even give her a hint, just kisses her on the jaw and says he’ll fix this. Fix what? That’s not a real hint.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Sir is kind of a jerk. I’m sorry, I’ll probably get spammed by fans but whatever. Sir gets mad at Meira for calling him father when she’s eight years old. I mean seriously, just explain it to her that you don’t want her to think of you like that, instead he gets all mad at her. Meira also says this which just really made me hurt for her in the matter of Sir: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I never wanted to fade into nothing, but Sir never told me I wouldn’t. He never let me believe I mattered to Winter beyond my responsibility to lead a normal, safe life once our kingdom was free from Angra, regardless of how fervently I tried to prove to him that I was more. He just let me think I would be lost in all this, that I wasn’t important enough to matter further.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> When Sir finally gives Meira some recognition, I feel it comes too late and it’s too small to really matter while Meira clings to compliment like it means everything. It actually made me sad for her.<br><br>Side characters: I’m sorry, but they kind of just drop off and are barely (if ever) heard from again. They never gain any real characterization. While I thought I’d get to know all the Winterian group Meira traveled with, I mean there’s less than ten of them, I’m left off with only really knowing three (one of them Meira). I felt like I knew more about Gregg and Crystalla who are only ever talked about in past tense. <br><br>Plot: Sadly, some parts of the book were just really predictable. A great amount of the plot is slowed by info dumps that occur nearly every chapter. Whether it be about the history, magic, and customs of the countries, there’s a lot of info dumps. Not all of them are bad, but I felt like some could have been shortened greatly. If it’s important for future novels, go further into it in the next novel because by the time I get through all these info dumps, I won’t remember it unless it mattered to this book’s plot. The overall plot appears to be pretty well thought out though, and for that I’m glad that it’s not forced. Though the scenery was pretty well described throughout the novel giving you a clear picture of the world (though I was also quite thankful to get the map at the beginning of the book to give me an idea of the land layout).<br><br>Expectations: I tried to keep my expectations really low for this book. I knew that just because Xena’s Chakram was on the front cover, it didn’t mean I would like the book. When I first read the synopsis, I didn’t even really want to read it, it didn’t sound like my cup of tea. Was I influenced by the Chakram on the front to buy this book? Um yeah! At the end of the day, do I feel like my expectations were met? Somewhat, but I’m still disappointed this didn’t ‘wow’ me.<br><br>This isn’t Xena Warrior Princess, I’ll give you all that much right now. If you’re looking for her, you’re better off marathoning episodes. At the end of the day though, Meira isn’t a bad character, she’s just missing that spark I need. Will I be reading the next one? (Honestly it depends on the cover. I’m kidding of course.) Since it took me this long to actually buy this one though, it may be a while before I decide to go out and buy the next one. <br><br>Overall, this isn't the greatest book out there, but it's also not the worst. To me, it's just okay. And I guess that is that: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423019845i/13577195._SY540_.jpg" width="392" height="532" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6946412796096177621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

FUCK.<br /><br />The words in capslock are obviously me screaming bc I have issues.<br /><br />*<br />*<br />*<br /><br /><s>The blurb sounds so good and the cover is so pretty and I swear to God, if this turns out to be a disappointment I'm going to cry in a corner and eat my doorknob while ripping the pages out of this book bc I'm SUPER pumped and excited for this.</s></span>

<div id="review_1236331323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1236331323" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1236331323?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1236331323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11051659225165886266">I probably would have rated this a tad lower, but (<i>
  <b>and I can't BELIEVE I'm saying this</b>
</i>) I adored the love triangle.<br/><b>I KNOW, RIGHT?!</b><br/>No one is as surprised by that statement as I am.<br/>And it <i>is</i> a love triangle. There's the boy she's loved all of her life, and then there's the boy she's forcibly engaged to. <br/>Guess which one I picked?<br/>The new guy!<br/>Again, no one is as surprised as I am. I'm a HUGE sucker for the We've-Been-Friends-Forever sort of love. Plus, there's no <i>easy winner</i> in this triangle. Lik</span>
  <span id="freeText11051659225165886266" style="display:none">I probably would have rated this a tad lower, but (<i>
  <b>and I can't BELIEVE I'm saying this</b>
</i>) I adored the love triangle.<br><b>I KNOW, RIGHT?!</b><br>No one is as surprised by that statement as I am.<br>And it <i>is</i> a love triangle. There's the boy she's loved all of her life, and then there's the boy she's forcibly engaged to. <br>Guess which one I picked?<br>The new guy!<br>Again, no one is as surprised as I am. I'm a HUGE sucker for the We've-Been-Friends-Forever sort of love. Plus, there's no <i>easy winner</i> in this triangle. Like, it doesn't turn out that Mr. Boy Next Door is hiding nefarious plans for world domination or anything. He's awesome, and he really loves her.<br>However, in the immortal words of the philosopher Beyonce...<br><i>
  <b>If you like it then you shoulda put a ring on it.</b>
</i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445295505ra/16625399.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nice world building in this one, as well. The concept of the world and it's brand of magic, while not new-new, had a nice flavor to it. <br>Ok. I'm going to be honest. I can't for the life of me figure out a way to describe the plot that sounds even remotely interesting. I've been staring at this page for several hours (read: minutes), and I'm coning up with a blank. Sorry.<br>There's magical relics, quests, a tough heroine, honorable princes, an evil villain, secrets, and dreams from a dead queen.<br>Read it for yourself if you want to know more.<br><br>I will say that at times my mind <i>did</i> wander a bit between action scenes, but that's typical for me because I have the attention span of a squirrel, and doesn't necessarily reflect poorly on the book. <br>My only quasi-complaint?<br>The <b>Big Twist</b> was something I guessed fairly early on, but that didn't really lessen my enjoyment of the story all that much. So, yeah...tiny annoyance.<br>This was (on the whole) an interesting book, and I had very few issues with it. If you've been sitting on the fence, go ahead and give it a shot.<br><br>Also reviewed for:<br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2015/04/review-snow-like-ashes-snow-like-ashes.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>

<div id="review_1395779247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1395779247" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1395779247?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062286932" href="/book/show/24331409-snow-like-ashes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395779247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer313736291742819549"><b>2.5<br/><br/>“I don’t need made-up strength. I’m strong enough on my own—me, Meira, no magic or conduit or anything.”</b><br/><br/>How is it then that you don't feel truly fulfilled until you find out that you after all ARE the special snowflake we all knew since page one you'd end up being?<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417351190ra/12307684.gif' width='420' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I hate this kind of plot development. The main character spends the entire story trying to find in him/herself a reason to feel important on his own, by virtue only of his spiritual or whatever strength, and then it turns out that </span>
  <span id="freeText313736291742819549" style="display:none"><b>2.5<br><br>“I don’t need made-up strength. I’m strong enough on my own—me, Meira, no magic or conduit or anything.”</b><br><br>How is it then that you don't feel truly fulfilled until you find out that you after all ARE the special snowflake we all knew since page one you'd end up being?<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417351190ra/12307684.gif" width="420" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I hate this kind of plot development. The main character spends the entire story trying to find in him/herself a reason to feel important on his own, by virtue only of his spiritual or whatever strength, and then it turns out that all this internal struggle was totally unnecessary because -oh, I'm a friggin' <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[queen and the magic you've been looking for in the past sixteen damn years it's in me because I AM <i>THAT</i> SPESHAL <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Yay.<br><br>It makes no sense, why do authors not get it? It wouldn't seem so ridiculous if the story wheeled on the 'peculiarity' of the protagonist since the beginning. At least be honest about what you want your story to be about. I in the first place love fantasy stories featuring a protagonist with astonishing abilities, but I can't help feeling pissed off when all his/her attempts to be strong and meaningful just for who (s)he is are frustrated by the <b>special snowflake syndrome</b>.<br><br>Of course there are some cases in which this situation is well-handled. This is not one of those cases. I hated how <b>Meira</b> (the MC) remarks that she feel like she managed to get Sir's (the man who raised her) attention only when she finds out what she finds out. Sir knew who she was since before, so he's always held her dear, of course, but the impression we get is that this poor girl was treated like a dirty rug for her whole life until she couldn't be treated like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the queen she's meant to be <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in broad daylight. I find this <b>offensive and disrespectful</b> and I don't even want to think about what kind of moral it, purposefully or not, conveys.<br><br>The only good thing I can say about the<b> plot</b> is that it's really <b>fast-paced</b> and so, if nothing, you don't have to add boredom to the <b>idiocy</b> and the <b>banalities</b> you already have to stand. <br><br>For one thing, I don't get why Mather and Meira had to be kept in the dark about their own identities. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why not tell them that the real boy-king is still alive but hidden somewhere else? Why let poor Mather think he's the king, why put all these responsibilities and fears on his shoulders just to come up then with 'sorry, it's a joke, Meira gets the crown'? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451308363ra/17526804.gif" width="700" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's just me or this thing is unbelievably cruel and tactless? I hope the next book will be about Mather's revenge. Despite how flat and flimsy his character is, he still deserves it.<br><br>But then again, the whole story if filled to the brim with nonsensical <i>escamotage</i>s like this, and I don't really want to go on like forever. I'll mention just another one and then I'll stop, I swear: when <b>Theron</b> deliberately walks into Spring's hands in order to push his father to react. I didn't know whether to cry or laugh. You doomed yourself to death on the belief that your heartless, horrible excuse of a father will move his army, thing that he never agreed to do, to get you back? And I thought you were intelligent <i>and</i> hot.<br><br>The <b>magic system</b> is one of the reasons I decided to read the book, because I'd heard it was really good, but then it proved to be a big meh. Not original, not convincing, not compelling, even confusing for lack of explanations. It is repeated hundreds and hundreds of time that the Conduits work only when they are on the lands they are tied to, and that they are tied to a bloodline and a gender, and that their power extends only to the citizens of the country they belong to. Fine. How does it work, exactly? It suffices to be born within the borders of that country or the whole thing is blood-related? And if it is blood-related, does this mean that in thousands of years (not my conjecture, Meira's words) the various peoples that live in this world have never mingled? Sorry, but I can't believe that. Too, far too simplistic. Unless the book provides me with a rational explanation, which it didn't.<br><br>And at last (I know you were waiting for this) the <b>love-triangle</b>. <br>Know that I am sighing. Repeatedly. In discouragement.<br>The truly sad thing is that without that horrible, embarrassing, let's-see-who-can-pee-further fighting scene it could have been even enjoyable. It's not as if Mather and Theron are intolerable. Mather, as I said, is annoyingly flat, but he's kind of fine, and Theron is absolutely likeable, although I stay firm in my opinion that insta-love must be declared illegal, unless you are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Lu</a>. If you are Marie Lu you can do whatever you want and still make it make sense (I don't even know if this sentence is grammatically correct). <br><br>Now, will I continue the series? Honestly, I don't know. I've heard Raasch made a mess with the second book and I don't know if it's worth the torture. I guess I'll see.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="313736291742819549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
