    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_898696141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/898696141" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/898696141?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=epic-battles">epic-battles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=huge-character-development">huge-character-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=awesome-romance">awesome-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=good-vs-bad">good-vs-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer898696141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15127015464338999615">Did I ever mention how much I love YA high fantasy? Because I do. Love it, I mean. I REALLY LOVE IT. But you know what I love even more than the genre itself? Finding a YA high fantasy book that I also enjoy, because those are so rare and precious. Well, fellow bookish people, I am happy to announce that I found another bejeweled novel that fits the bill perfectly -- <i>Snow Like Ashes</i> by Sara Raasch. Let the fangirling commence. <i>*jumps up and down excitedly*</i><br/><br/>First of all, I gotta say <i>Snow Like Ashe</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15127015464338999615" style="display:none">Did I ever mention how much I love YA high fantasy? Because I do. Love it, I mean. I REALLY LOVE IT. But you know what I love even more than the genre itself? Finding a YA high fantasy book that I also enjoy, because those are so rare and precious. Well, fellow bookish people, I am happy to announce that I found another bejeweled novel that fits the bill perfectly -- <i>Snow Like Ashes</i> by Sara Raasch. Let the fangirling commence. <i>*jumps up and down excitedly*</i><br><br>First of all, I gotta say <i>Snow Like Ashes</i> not only has a glorious title, but that its cover is real awesomeness. Just look at that pretty thing! Don't you wanna pet it? <br><br>Second of all, this book resembled on some level the <i>Throne of Glass</i> series and I got serious <i>The Winner's Crime</i> vibes. But besides those deja-vu sensations, I have to say <i>Snow Like Ashes</i> had a bit of everything from the tales we've come to love: the burden of a young monarch that has to rebuild a crushed kingdom, too many vile kings to keep count, a touch of magic and a gloriously fierce heroine you cannot help than cheer for. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-sWsQcge-9UM/VY_xxurgdTI/AAAAAAAAPEY/d-IZOw4A2Gc/s1600/9031775.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="168" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435497131ra/15353296.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The story centers on eight Winterians, the last people of the Winter kingdom, one of the eight kingdoms ruling the world of Primoria. Sixteen years ago, Winter was shattered by an attack made by Spring, one that left in its wake only ruins, slaves and the feeble hope that those survivors will somehow manage to get back the kingdom's conduit -- the land's source of magic -- and rebuilt their long lost home. Among these eight survivors are two fateful figures: Mather, the future king of Winter, and Meira, a warrior girl through and through that also happens to be our heroine. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Someday we will be more than words in the dark.”</b>
</i><br><br>Of course, that was the plot summarized in a few words but there are bits and pieces that proved to be a tad more complicated and will surely become a delight once you read them. The journey was full of imaginative turns, although I have to admit I was able to predict some of the bigger surprises. Regardless, the plot itself had a lot of ramifications that readers couldn't anticipate because the world presented to us was still yet unknown, so that was a source of constant eagerness and thrilling fascination. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-TSKevDEFfJ8/VY_xzYCn1oI/AAAAAAAAPEs/6_PxNLUYy0Q/s1600/unconditionallove02.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435497131i/15353297.jpg" width="245" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved Meira. I'd describe her as a mix of Celaena and Kestrel, but with a big dose of childishness in her. Not necessarily an immature teenager, but definitely quite independent (a trait that has a tendency to turn into infuriating stubbornness) and impulsive. Thank gods she's clever. Couple that with the fact that she's fierce and stubbornly witty and you got yourself a new Elsa with a vengeance streak and protective behavior. I reveled in her character-development, because by the end of the book she became an incredibly brave young woman that finally realized the important matters at hand. Plus, I love a girl who knows how to humor her way into conflicts and what-nots. <br><br>You know what's next, don't you? The juicy part, the sigh-inducing element, the key aspect of a great read for fangirls everywhere -- the romance. And I'm telling you, start hyperventilating ‘cause we have a serious case of drooling bound to begin upon reading <i>Snow Like Ashes</i>. <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-WgE9ISyIKlk/VY_xy3OjX2I/AAAAAAAAPE8/Q9h-vpSXH3w/s1600/tumblr_mmata4iZHa1s751i1o1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="172" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435497131ra/15353298.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There's Mather, the one that Meira is basically smitten about since she knows herself. Then there's Theron, a new guy that had me at hello. Yeah, I wasn't really Mather's fan because I kept imagining Tommen from <i>Game of Thrones</i> as the incapable kings they both are, but I guess he does have some lovable qualities, such as having a gorgeous body and all. Plus, he's royalty -- that has to count up for something, doesn't it? <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-LhqaRStUwWY/VY_x0MlgZnI/AAAAAAAAPE4/YmUf1TLaG-s/s1600/westley.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="174" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435497131i/15353299.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But it doesn't matter because Theron is crown prince, so potato potato. And this guy, lemme just tell you, practically waltzed straight into my heart and into Meira's with his bookish personality (Dorian alarm, srsly), warrior skills, snark-filled banter tendency and unconditional devotion. All that and a handsome face and an even more gorgeous body. <b>IS HE FOR REAL? I LOVE HIM.</b> <i>*drools*</i> <br><br><i>
  <b>“I want to be someone worthy of my kingdom. I want to be someone worthy of you.”</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-n1cpvcG4MdI/VY_xyd-ewqI/AAAAAAAAPFA/QyThK8g7N4M/s1600/d36aa09560ae707040d1d83f59441c2c.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435497131i/15353300.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>No, Andreea, he actually isn't. </i>&lt;-- that was a sad afterthought. <br><br>Coming back to the romance aspect, I was afraid it would turn into an annoying and tiring love-triangle when obviously there was no need for it. BUT IT DIDN'T. <i>*happy dance*</i> I was so goddamn excited to see a mature choice unfolding for once (hear me, Leigh Bardugo?), to finally let the sappy, childhood romance dissolve so that the real love can take its course, even though it was unexpected. This created a sweet relationship between Theron and Meira that had me giggling and smiling with my whole face. The whole situation better stay like this (Team Theron all the way), because otherwise Sara Raasch will have a furious shipper here. <br><br><i>
  <b>“He drops his grin into a pout, puckering his lips and pulling his eyebrows tight over his nose.<br>I glare.<br>He pouts harder.<br>“You’re impossible,” I growl, and rip open the book.<br>Theron laughs and scoots a little closer to me. “Impossible, endearing. Synonyms, really.”</b>
</i><br><br>Some secondary characters were more developed than others and, of course, I loved those more. Sir William Loren was hands-down the father-figure and everyone is sure to love his wise, brave and loyal self. There's even a chance to drop a few tears at some point, courtesy of Sir. I especially liked the relationship between him and Meira, the girl's unwavering respect for him. Then there's Hannah, which was honestly an equivalent for Elena from ToG, whom I tolerated even though she could've been more straight-forward for the sake of the rest of the characters. And I liked Nessa, Rose and Mona, so fingers crossed we'll be spending more time with them. Noam is an egoistical, vain douche-bag, Herod the sick monster (=Cain) and Angra the power-hungry lunatic. Ah, well, there should be some leeches, I guess. <br><br>The world-building was one of my favorite parts of the whole book. The idea of having four Rhythm kingdoms (ones that transcended the 4 seasons annually) and four Season kingdoms (ones that kept their defining season all year long) instantly grabbed my attention. I kept going back to the notion of Season Courts from Fae inspired books (ACoTaR reminiscence), but this time the concept was expanded on a bigger level. I loved the people, the traditions, the different ideologies and perhaps most of all the sense of patriotism that connected all characters. Hopefully, we'll get to see the rest of the kingdoms in the following installments, seeing that every one of them is equally entrancing and crazy in their own way. BRING ON THE AWESOMENESS (AND THE SHIRTLESS SOLDIERS) CAUSE I AM READY.<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-i3uvCNzzL0Q/VY_xyLrBgtI/AAAAAAAAPEk/nKqVaYeHvVA/s1600/10657279.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="160" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435497131ra/15353301.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Snow Like Ashes</i> ended on a cheerful and (temporarily) peaceful note. All is not right in the world, but it's getting there one step at a time. The last image caught on my retina is a gorgeously winter wonderland that brought out all the heartwarming feelings my brain could muster that ensured that I'll close the book with a big idiotic grin, satisfied (no cliffy yay), yet demanding for the sequel at the same time (a girl wants to know what happens next). <br><br>My only complaint would be the somewhat fast pace. I am a fan of action-packed stories, but I felt that, if given more pages and maybe even split into half afterwards, the story up until this point could've been given so much more substance. In one second this happened and then this happened and then that and now this -- these events honestly could've spanned the plot of more books without it feeling a bit rushed. Maybe I just needed the respiro times between the big deals to be more developed or perhaps more details on key-elements, such as the Cordell kingdom. But the thing is that I still needed something. The story was a golden mine of potential and Sara Raasch delivered a captivating tale, but there was room for complexity, for grandness, for more. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-jtu9pqaz1zU/VY_xyKHlegI/AAAAAAAAPEc/nbsIE-XLIng/s1600/cldhvbnbetter.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435497131ra/15353302.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sara Raasch -- I'm officially a fan of hers. I knew I would like her and this book from the dedication in the beginning of the novel, because if that's not an example of determination and ambition, I don't know what is. Her writing style was quite curious since it seemed to blend a high fantasy atmosphere with daily language -- surprisingly, the combo worked. <br><br>So, book lovers everywhere. I've seen lots of so-and-so reviews for this title, but I honestly say that I'm with the bunch that tremendously enjoyed <i>Snow Like Ashes</i> and I urge you to give it a try. I read it cover-to-cover and I was kept at the edge of my seat, my toes curling at the sweet romance and my heart going all battlecry mode while cheering for the spunky heroine and her lot of fearless Winterians. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Even the strongest blizzard starts with a single snowflake.”</b>
</i><br><br>Now, October, please come quicker so I can have more Theron in my life. I won't mind if you kill the rest of the characters as long as you keep him safe, but I guess he'd be a bit upset so whatever. Gimme <i>Ice Like Fire</i> (I'm not below begging, Edelweiss)! <br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3<br><br>P.S.:</b> I have a feeling that the title for the 3rd book will start with Frost, because Meira said once "Snow and ice and frost above" and I was like BINGO. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15127015464338999615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1549966519?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" href="/user/show/52207144">♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ</a>

        rated it

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1549966519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5434124291014404953"><u>4 Snow Above! ★'s</u> <br/><br/><i>“Even the strongest blizzards start with a single snowflake.”</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521598972ra/25248094.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>“Holding on to some part of your past even if it means also holding on to the pain of never again having it. That pain is less horrible than the pain of forgetting.”</i> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521598523i/25248079._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>*Some minor spoilers may ensue*</b><br/><br/>Reread <3<br/>This is my second time reading "Snow Like Ashes" and though it does starts out slow, once I get to a certain part, I'm hooked! I have a hard time putting this book down. It's a real page turner ;)!! I was very intri</span>
  <span id="freeText5434124291014404953" style="display:none"><u>4 Snow Above! ★'s</u> <br><br><i>“Even the strongest blizzards start with a single snowflake.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521598972ra/25248094.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“Holding on to some part of your past even if it means also holding on to the pain of never again having it. That pain is less horrible than the pain of forgetting.”</i> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521598523i/25248079._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>*Some minor spoilers may ensue*</b><br><br>Reread &lt;3<br>This is my second time reading "Snow Like Ashes" and though it does starts out slow, once I get to a certain part, I'm hooked! I have a hard time putting this book down. It's a real page turner ;)!! I was very intrigued by this world Sara Raasch has created. I love magic... Magic is everything!! I really enjoy the story-line, the world-building, the writing style and of course the characters are amazing. They are easy to relate to and falling for them is effortless. Though the twists and turns throughout are pretty predictable, it is still so wonderfully addicting :D I like that the source of their magic comes from conduits. There are a total of eight. Witch include a- Locket, Staff, Cuff, Ring, Dagger, Ax(e), Crown and Shield. There are four Season Kingdoms and four Rhythm Kingdoms. All of which have long since been prejudiced towards one another. I also love that the people resemble the Season/Rhythm in-witch they come from. <b>For example:</b> Winterians have white hair, very pale skin, and bright blue eyes. Spring have blond hair, green eyes, and skin a little darker than Winterians. Summerians have hair red as fire, skin a creamy tan and eyes the color of liquid brown. Autumnians are copper-skinned, black hair and vibrant blue eyes. Cordellans usually have golden brown hair, brown eyes and light skin, though not as pale as Winterians, etc...<br><br>I love strong, fearless, bad-ass heroines and I got that with Meira. She's just so brave and very determined. And will do whats necessary to help free the Winterians form slavery, take back Winter and bring them home. She's gonna have a long road ahead of her. Good thing she has Mather the "future king" of Winter. Mather is confident, strong, great at combat, attractive and a really great guy. He's also Meira's best and closest friend. They grew up together, trained together, got into trouble together and both have feelings for one another ;) And then you have Theron the prince of Cordell. He's very sweet, attractive, always hits his mark, though, his people respect him and Theron and Meira are to be married. So if you despise <i>love triangles</i> this may not be for you! But for the record, I'm <b>Team♥MATHER!!!</b> Always &amp; forever :D Honestly though, I really enjoyed all the characters- Sir, Alysson, Dendera, Finn, Greer, Nessa, Conall, Garrigan, they are all fantastic!<br><br>If you have not had the chance to read this, I recommend that you do A-SAP! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521598523i/25248079._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“Sometimes placing our belief in something bigger than ourselves helps us get to a point where we can be enough on our own, magic or no magic.”</i> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521603024ra/25248345.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521598523i/25248079._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“I’m Hannah’s daughter. I’m Winter’s conduit. I’m a warrior, a soldier, a lady, a queen, and most of all, as I plunge across the snowfield toward Jannuari’s silent ruin, I’m Meira.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521603486ra/25248367.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5434124291014404953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1418677941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1418677941" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1418677941?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1418677941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15780703919657084167">******************** 4.5 STARS ********************<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Someday we will be more than words in the dark."</i>
</b><br/><br/>This book really surprised me! I didn't really think I'd enjoy Snow Like Ashes because all the reviews seemed to range from mixed to just plain average. I just ended up putting this series off until now because the premise honestly sounded so interesting and I figured I should just form my own opinion and see for myself how I'd like this book.<br/><br/>At first, I thought that the beginning was a little</span>
  <span id="freeText15780703919657084167" style="display:none">******************** 4.5 STARS ********************<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Someday we will be more than words in the dark."</i>
</b><br /><br />This book really surprised me! I didn't really think I'd enjoy Snow Like Ashes because all the reviews seemed to range from mixed to just plain average. I just ended up putting this series off until now because the premise honestly sounded so interesting and I figured I should just form my own opinion and see for myself how I'd like this book.<br /><br />At first, I thought that the beginning was a little <b>
  <i>slow and info-dumpy.</i>
</b> I was starting to get a little bored because nothing interesting was really happening. Although the story took awhile to progress, things turned around for me once we got to Cordell. And that ending though. <b>HOLY CRAP.</b> The last 50 pages was crazy! I was practically almost skimming because I was so eager to know what happened next lol.<br /><br /><b>I LOVED THE SEASONS/RHYTHM WORLD.</b> The world building was definitely one of my favorite aspects of the book. I just loved how one half of Primoria is ruled by Seasons and the other by Rhythms. But I also loved how certain magical conduits can only be used by the proper gender to ensure a balance of power between men and women. And all the poor Winterians. <i>Oh, my heart.</i> My heart broke for them so many times. I just loved everything about them. Their bravery, their perseverance. I literally had <b>goosebumps</b> just reading everything that the Winterians had to go through and what they did to keep their kingdom alive through their memories. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>I LOVED OUR MAIN CHARACTER MEIRA.</b> I really enjoyed Meira's character. Not everybody was constantly praising her beauty. Not everyone was falling head over heels for her. And most importantly, not everyone was putting her on a pedestal and constantly kissing her ass. <b>
  <i>So in short, she's not like Celaena Sardothien lol.</i>
</b> I felt like she was more real. More human. Less perfect. But it's those qualities that made Meira such a great character in the first place.<br /><br /><b>THERE'S A LOVE TRIANGLE.</b> But I found myself not minding it as much as I thought I would. In fact, I was even sort of relieved. I never knew we'd have a love triangle in the story prior to reading the book because there wasn't too much buzz about it. I wasn't a big fan of Meira and Mather. Their relationship felt too ordinary to me. It's like I've heard this type of romance before in about a billion other books and movies. Contrary to numerous opinions, I love romance in books. I think it adds the cherry on top of a perfect book. So while people are complaining, <i>"This better not have any romance in it"</i>, I'm just shouting, <b>
  <i>"YES YES YES."</i>
</b> :D So I was actually glad that Theron, <i>my baby</i>, came into the picture. I'm 100% on <b>
  <u>TEAM THERON.</u>
</b> Who doesn't want a badass prince who has a great body, great aim (with weapons guys xD), but who also has a softer artistic side to him? Not to mention, he has a personal relationship with his people. He knows them by name and what's going on in their lives. Mather doesn't count because he only had seven Winterians to worry about LOL. Theron is just perfect. So if Meira passes this opportunity up, <b>
  <i>I'll gladly marry Theron for her. ;)</i>
</b><br /><br />Now that I finally finished Snow Like Ashes, I'm a little worried about <b>
  <i>Ice Like Fire.</i>
</b> I've heard that it's definitely not as good as the first book and now I don't think I want to read the sequel. But I'm hoping Ice Like Fire just came down with second book syndrome, and the rest of the story will come together perfectly in the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15780703919657084167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer179947094548735273"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414333881i/11641254._SX540_.png' alt=' photo Banner_SnowLikeAshes_zps60f7fa03.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Every time someone asks me about <em>Throne of Glass</em>, I want to chuck <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> at their faces and yell something along the lines of, "Read this thing instead!" Of course, people won't listen to me if I don't justify my suggestion. Here's why I recommend everyone should pick up Snow Like Ashes:<br/><br/><b>Meira knows how to kick ass.</b><br/><br/><blockquote>“No matter what happens, no matter who turns on me, no matter what pompous swine thinks he has power over me, I am still me. I will always be me.”</blockquote><br/><br/>All her life, all Meira w</span>
  <span id="freeText179947094548735273" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414333881i/11641254._SX540_.png" alt=" photo Banner_SnowLikeAshes_zps60f7fa03.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Every time someone asks me about <em>Throne of Glass</em>, I want to chuck <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> at their faces and yell something along the lines of, "Read this thing instead!" Of course, people won't listen to me if I don't justify my suggestion. Here's why I recommend everyone should pick up Snow Like Ashes:<br><br><b>Meira knows how to kick ass.</b><br><br><blockquote>“No matter what happens, no matter who turns on me, no matter what pompous swine thinks he has power over me, I am still me. I will always be me.”</blockquote><br><br>All her life, all Meira wanted was to become a soldier. A fighter. Someone worthy enough to protect the kingdom she loves so much. She doesn't just want to be a pretty display--she wants to work, and she wants to be deserving of all the things she's been given credit for. <strong>Fierce, loyal and protective, Meira's your girl.</strong><br><br><b><em>Snow Like Ashes</em> is high fantasy at its best.</b><br><br>I have always been a fan of high fantasy novels. I just love being drawn into new worlds with all sorts of magic and sorcery around. <strong>Raasch definitely succeeded in creating a wondrous new world</strong>, yet making everything easy to remember and easy to understand. You might be scared to find out that there are eight different kingdoms, but worry not!<strong> The author puts everything down simply and sufficiently</strong>.<br><br><b>Be still, my poor little fangirl heart!</b><br><br>I would be crazy not to mention all the feels I got from reading this book, because HELLO MATHER.<strong> I was practically in love with this guy since chapter one.</strong> Personally, I thought he and Meira and some wonderful chemistry, and I squealed to my heart's delight each time they would have a scene together.<br><br><b>Yeah, there is this other guy...</b><br><br>Okay, so, there is a love triangle. The guy on the other side is Theron. <strong>He's definitely a nice, kind one, but for some reason I couldn't feel anything for him</strong>. I was pretty <em>meh</em> every time the guy showed up. I don't hate the guy or anything, I'm just saying that, if by any chance he would, say, get eaten by a bunch of wild piranhas, I wouldn't really care. And yes, I instantly root for the guy the heroine's known longer, and that's Mather in this case. It just seems more believable for me.<br><br><b>Raasch knows how to write.</b><br><br><blockquote>“Someday we will be more than words in the dark.”</blockquote><br><br>It was really easy for me to get into Raasch's writing. <strong>I flew through the pages almost giddily, really.</strong> I guess there were a few twists I discovered a bit early, but for the most part, I was on my toes, itching to find out what will happen to Meira, Mather and Sir <del>and not Theron</del>.<strong> I also loved that Raasch incorporated family into the story.</strong> Sir was like a father-figure to everyone, and I love how they all respected him, and how he gave them care and support in return.</span>
  <a data-text-id="179947094548735273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1430950780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430950780" />
    <a title="Lia  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48295288-lia"><img alt="Lia  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594824825p2/48295288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430950780?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia  " href="/user/show/48295288-lia">Lia  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=magic-and-supernatural-things">magic-and-supernatural-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=the-hype-is-a-liarrr">the-hype-is-a-liarrr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=english-and-american-lit-and-more">english-and-american-lit-and-more</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430950780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6191450670777012572"><u>1.5 stars</u><br/><br/><br/>Well, this was underwhelming as heck.<br/><br/>First things first: with this review, I don't mean to say that this is a bad book, because it's not. In fact, I can see why so many people loved it, but it definitely wasn't for me. It was just so generic and bland, and was completely identical to every other fantasy novel I've read before. Nothing about it was remarkable. <br/>I found the whole seasons idea to be quite silly: what is it with authors these days, that they keep naming things after seasons,</span>
  <span id="freeText6191450670777012572" style="display:none"><u>1.5 stars</u><br><br><br>Well, this was underwhelming as heck.<br><br>First things first: with this review, I don't mean to say that this is a bad book, because it's not. In fact, I can see why so many people loved it, but it definitely wasn't for me. It was just so generic and bland, and was completely identical to every other fantasy novel I've read before. Nothing about it was remarkable. <br>I found the whole seasons idea to be quite silly: what is it with authors these days, that they keep naming things after seasons, colors (yes, The Darkest Minds) or numbers (yes, The Selection)? How effin' CREATIVE of you.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383089298ra/6383798.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book's main problem was basically its utter lack of originality. There is a kingdom that has been destroyed by a generic villain, a magic system that makes very little sense (okay, I get it, it's <i>magic</i>. But still.) and really boring characters. Meira, the main character, was the most interesting one of the lot - but then of course she had to be a super special snowflake and everything that made her fascinating just disappeared. Awesome. As for the other characters... I really have no idea what to say, since I can barely remember their names. They did not have their own personality, but they existed only when they interacted with Meira, and I have very mixed feelings about the love interests (yes, plural). I couldn't stand Mather, the great warrior and soon-to-be-king who thought so damn highly of himself. Meira's fascination with him made no sense to me, and whenever his name popped out on the page I let out an exasperated sigh because NO MORE PLEASE. Theron, on the other hand, was quite likable. He was kind and smart, but again, really generic (you'll have to excuse my repetition of the word, but it's the only way I can describe this book). I liked him because there was nothing not to like about him, but he had no real depth as a character. <br>As for the plot, I feel like I just read 400 pages of nothing. It was quite hard for me not to DNF the book, because a) the characters just... They kept traveling from one place to another. They were constantly on the run, and it felt like a big series of different situations and a million of different subplots. Annoying., and b) the info-dumps. They were one of the main things that prevented me from enjoying the book. There were countless pages explaining how everything worked, and it was repetitive and boring. I found myself skipping entire paragraphs and even whole pages because I was too bored to keep reading.<br>The ending was predictable and as underwhelming as the rest of the book. I feel like Snow Like Ashes had great potential but was executed really poorly, with average writing, boring characters and a plot that was going nowhere. My favorite scenes were actually the (few) more light-hearted scenes at king Noam's palace, and I think Raasch does much better with friendly banter than she does when she attempts to write epic battles and meaningful conversations that end up bordering on overdramatic.<br> <br>Then again, don't let my review discourage you. I still think a lot of people are going to enjoy this book, but if you've read a lot of YA fantasy and you're sick of seeing the same things happen all over again, Snow Like Ashes might not be the right book for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6191450670777012572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1322357830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1322357830" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1322357830?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=your-spesual-is-showing">your-spesual-is-showing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322357830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12106097714131428901"><blockquote>
  <i>"I can feel him eyeing Mather, both of them caught in an awkward web surrounding me. I'm at the center of a weird possessive feud between the Winter king and the Cordellan prince. How in the name of all that is cold did that happen?"</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438949569ra/15773313.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have no idea. But of course, no love triangle is complete without <b>manly preening! </b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"It whacks into the center of the target, the handle wobbling from force. <br/><br/>Theron turns to me, half his face slight with the beginnings of a smile. "My weapon of choice doesn't </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12106097714131428901" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I can feel him eyeing Mather, both of them caught in an awkward web surrounding me. I'm at the center of a weird possessive feud between the Winter king and the Cordellan prince. How in the name of all that is cold did that happen?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438949569ra/15773313.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have no idea. But of course, no love triangle is complete without <b>manly preening! </b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"It whacks into the center of the target, the handle wobbling from force. <br><br>Theron turns to me, half his face slight with the beginnings of a smile. "My weapon of choice doesn't matter," he says, continuing our conversation like nothing happened. His eyes flash to Mather over my shoulder. "No matter what, I always hit my mark."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438949569ra/15773314.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To be fair, Meira doesn't spent a lot of time mooning over Boy 1 and Boy 2. <br><br>Her country, Winter, was destroyed by Spring several years ago and the handful of them not in work camps live in constant fear, moving from one place to the next. Their only hope is that the boy king, Mathe, escaped with them and someday, they might find the magic conduit that Angra stole from them and they can rebuild their lives. <br><br>Sounds pretty awesome, right? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438949569ra/15773315.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The premise reminds me of Avatar the Last Airbender. The Fire Nation wiped out the Air Nomads except for Aang and now, he has to defeat them. Also like Avatar, Snow Like Ashes' world is split into four countries: Spring, Summer, Autumn, and Winter. <br><br>Only female heirs can use magic, which is pretty awesome. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Though in hindsight, it's used to facilitate the twist that Meira is Hannah's daughter, which is less awesome. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438949569ra/15773316.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the <i>writing</i>, guys. I've figured out why YA Fantasy and I don't gel. Most of it is written in smothering <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor" title="Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Laini Taylor</a> prose and it makes me feel like I'm wading through a pool of syrup. I keep kicking out my arms and legs, looking for something substantial to hold onto, but it's gooey mush. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438949569ra/15773317.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not bad per se--it's actually quite good--but just not for me. The story isn't interesting enough to make up for the writing. <br><br>Info-dumps plague the narrative in the worst way. When Meira first arrives in Spring, she hears someone curse, "Golden leaves," then proceeds to spend a big, unnecessary paragraph explaining it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Just as Winter focused its magic on mining, Coredell focuses its conduit on opportunity--on helping its citizenswork a situation in their favor so they get the most out of it. Opportunistic, resourceful, swindlers: whatever they're called, they can make "leaves turn to gold"--a Cordellan phrase Sir explained in our many lessons, referring to the fact that they're so good at turning a profit it's as if they make leaves on a tree turn into gold coins. That explains Captain Dominick's curse earlier--golden leaves."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438949569ra/15773318.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Plus, I saw the twist coming miles away. <br><br>Will others like Snow Like Ashes? Maybe. But it just didn't click with me. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_660790666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660790666" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/660790666?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=lovely-romance-but-not-central">lovely-romance-but-not-central</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=finding-oneself">finding-oneself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=heartwrenching">heartwrenching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-hero">good-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-heroine">good-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=haunting-narration">haunting-narration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=packs-a-punch">packs-a-punch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=no-instalove">no-instalove</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660790666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9801134041448370897"><strong>Holy Jesus in a manger on the 25th of December... I think I just found a new fantasy series to love.</strong><br/><br/>And here I thought the Young Adult demographic has forgotten to churn out awesome high fantasies. The last time I've ever loved a YA Fantasy with a female heroine this much was when I read <em>The Girl of Fire and Thorns Trilogy</em> by Rae Carson. Since then, the fantasies I've read didn't even ignite any wonder or awe in me, didn't make me feel as immersed, didn't make me feel as involved or as engrossed</span>
  <span id="freeText9801134041448370897" style="display:none"><strong>Holy Jesus in a manger on the 25th of December... I think I just found a new fantasy series to love.</strong><br><br>And here I thought the Young Adult demographic has forgotten to churn out awesome high fantasies. The last time I've ever loved a YA Fantasy with a female heroine this much was when I read <em>The Girl of Fire and Thorns Trilogy</em> by Rae Carson. Since then, the fantasies I've read didn't even ignite any wonder or awe in me, didn't make me feel as immersed, didn't make me feel as involved or as engrossed. They paled in comparison and I was left to looking at non-YA fantasy books to give me my fix (hi, Brandon Sanderson!).<br><br>And then I read this beautiful book. <strong><em>Snow Like Ashes</em> reminded me of the beauty of a fantastical setting, of a heroine who struggles with herself while finding her place in a bleak and confusing world, of finding courage from the most unexpected of places. </strong>To say that I loved this is an understatement - I adored it! It perfected the formula that I mentally concocted to myself when it comes to evaluating the epicness of a fantasy book.<br><br>* Is this a book with good world-building?<strong> YES!<br></strong>* Is this a book that doesn't have an overwhelming romance?<strong> YES!<br></strong>* Is this a book that portray deep and complex relationships and conflicts?<strong> YES!<br>* </strong>Is this a book with a strong heroine? <strong>YES!<br></strong>* Is this a book with a strong and <em>relatable</em> heroine? <strong>YES!<br></strong>* Is this a book with a strong and relatable heroine <em>that also undergoes massive character development? <strong>YES!<br></strong></em>* Is this a book with a strong and relatable -- <strong>FUCK IT ALREADY YES YES YES YES TO EVERYTHING!</strong><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416396094ra/11952337.gif" alt="" width="400" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can you feel my enthusiasm? I truly do love this book, I do. If that's not enough to convince you, I don't know what will. But in case it doesn't (I am mentally shaking my head here!), I will list the reasons in extensive detail on WHY YOU SHOULD READ THIS BOOK:<br><br><strong>First of all, the world-building. I loved it so much.</strong> There are eight kingdoms, four that are Rhythm (in which they all experience all the seasons in a year) and four that are Seasons (in which each is eternally in one season for all year long - Spring, Summer, Autumn, and Winter). Usually, I see something like this, I somehow raise an eyebrow because there is a tendency for this to feel "cheesy". <strong>But Raasch was able to weave a setting in which every kingdom and every citizen from their respective kingdoms are different from each other and have characteristics of their own that they can truly call theirs. </strong>I loved how everything was so unique, having their own delicacies (frozen berries! YUM!) to having their own unique appearances (white hair and blue eyes...?! I need to draw this!). <strong>It definitely helped that Raasch is a terribly good writer. She can weave words and descriptions so intricately that I was able to imagine myself being surrounded by the world to the minute detail</strong> - I could somehow feel the cold of Winter, the happiness of the people in Bithai as they greeted their soldiers, the bleak atmosphere in Abril as slaves milled about defeatedly.<br><br><strong>And the heroine! I absolutely loved Meira. I loved how she was such a complex character who had a lot of issues inside her that I could relate and emphathize with. </strong>She wasn't a doormat, and she knew what she wanted and she knew what needed to be done, and I loved how throughout the novel, we get to witness how she struggled to balance both of them, how to serve her country without losing an integral part of her, and how she realized later on the stakes and how to achieve the freedom they have sought for sixteen years.  <strong>She was incredibly layered, and even though she had moments of angst, they never felt overwhelming and over-the-top - she just really felt genuine and human. </strong>And did I mention how she's a strong, independent girl? I loved all sides of her, and she even has beaten Celaena Sardothien from Throne of Glass in the "Kick-Ass" category.<br><br><strong>And her relationships with everyone were as complex as well, especially with Sir. </strong>Usually, the only complex relationships we get are between MCs and their love interests, so this one was such a nice change - a relationship between that of a "father" and a "daughter", of a "superior" and a "soldier", one who continuously tries to seek the other's approval. I may or may not have shed a tear during a scene with both of them while reading (hint: I actually cried).<br><br>And the romance? <strong>I loved how it didn't overtake the story. I loved how the story didn't revolve around it. I loved how it stayed in the background and strengthened the characters rather than took the controls of the plot.</strong> This is the kind of romance that I live for - one that isn't so "in-your-face" and relies on gestures and subtlety to tickle your heart. Even though it's a love triangle, I didn't mind, because it wasn't a romance that demands your full attention; it wasn't a romance in which we <em>have</em> to side with Guy A or Guy B - it was a romance in which we are simply <em>TEAM MEIRA! </em><br><br>(In any case, the book makes it hard for you to choose anyway, because both guys are awesome people with kind hearts and good intentions. And Meira isn't all over them like a lovestruck fool, making it a better experience. It truly reminds me of Rae Carson's series in this aspect, because in that one, we don't truly get to know who the main love interest is until the second book.)<br><br><strong>So what did we learn here, ladies and gents? It's that <em>Snow Like Ashes</em> is a goddamn good book and you need to buy it and read it and treasure it forever and ever. </strong><br><br>Amen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9801134041448370897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1080708597" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080708597" />
    <a title="Aly (In Wonderland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22178203-aly-in-wonderland"><img alt="Aly (In Wonderland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552929589p2/22178203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1080708597?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (In Wonderland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (In Wonderland)" href="/user/show/22178203-aly-in-wonderland">Aly (In Wonderland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062286949" href="/book/show/20602999-snow-like-ashes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080708597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18316906456920169960"><i>
  <blockquote>"Someday, we will be more than words in the dark."</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>For a long time, YA Fantasy was repetitive and boring, with the same special snowflakes, the same innocent, pure heroines. All the stories were formulaic, as if it wasn’t physically possible to write anything different.<br/><br/>Lately, though, <b>YA fantasy has started branching out.</b> It was easily forgotten how much this reader loved the magic and forbidden love stories, the strange creatures that lurked in the dark, the different kingdoms, the results o</span>
  <span id="freeText18316906456920169960" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"Someday, we will be more than words in the dark."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />For a long time, YA Fantasy was repetitive and boring, with the same special snowflakes, the same innocent, pure heroines. All the stories were formulaic, as if it wasn’t physically possible to write anything different.<br /><br />Lately, though, <b>YA fantasy has started branching out.</b> It was easily forgotten how much this reader loved the magic and forbidden love stories, the strange creatures that lurked in the dark, the different kingdoms, the results of a beautiful imagination. Snow Like Ashes, even though it followed the “special snowflake” trope, was all of the above and more.<br /><br />Meira is a Winteranian soldier, one of the twenty-five survivors that escaped the night Angra, King of Spring, invaded. Now there are only eight survivors, and the race to piecing the locket holding all of Winter’s power is tighter than ever. Angra has one half, and the second half is floating, waiting to be grabbed. When Meira is entrusted with the mission to recover the floating half, she can’t believe her luck. Finally, she can show Sir just how good she is!<br /><br />Once the locket pieces are restored, Mather, the love interest and prince of Winter, can return to his rightful place on the throne and free the Winteranians from the brutal work camps run by the ruthless Angra. However, things are not quite as they seem and, as Meira and her friends embark on another journey, she’s going to find out just how difficult it is to really be “free.”<br /><br /><b>There is a love triangle.</b> I don’t mind. <b>Meira is a special snowflake.</b> I don’t mind. <b>There’s, sometimes, a bit of deus ex machina at work.</b> <i>I don’t mind.</i> Raasch weaves a story of mystery and love, betrayal and strength, so well that it sweeps you up and carries you on. I found myself sitting down with this book in the morning and finishing it in the evening. It is that good.<br /><br />I loved the idea that the seasons were kingdoms, and each kingdom’s cities had names based after the months in the respective seasons. For example, Abril, Jannuari, Oktuber. I also loved the humour in the story — there wasn’t too much to take away from the severity of the cause, but there wasn’t little enough to make the story drag. Theron and Meira like to banter, and it’s sweet and funny.<br /><br />When Mather and Theron both try to prove their worth, it’s not only funny but also interesting to see Meira pull away from the love that cannot be and free herself of it. It’s nice to see a heroine grow into her role, and take on bigger responsibilities, shirking the ideas of “I just wanna be me”.<br /><br /><b>Yes, some of it is highly predictable</b> but there are also some twists and turns that take you completely by surprise. Ice Like Fire, book 2 in this astounding trilogy, is one of the most highly anticipated reads of 2015.<br /><br /><a href="http://magazine.100percentrock.com/reviews/book-reviews/201509/98810" rel="nofollow noopener">This review is now LIVE on 100% Rock!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18316906456920169960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_870916447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/870916447" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/870916447?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer870916447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12855092661899959006">OH BREAK OUT THE CELEBRATORY POPSICLES! <b>THIS WAS ABSOLUTELY INCREDIBLE!</b> I feel the need to flail excessively because this was a super highly anticipated read for me. And it did. not. disappoint. YAY AND FINALLY. So let's make snow angels and hug icicles because I LOVE THIS BOOK.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427512468ra/14278950.gif' width='245' height='175' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But, also, I have logical things to say. (Aren't you glad? I know you are, stop rolling your eyes.)<br/><br/><b>SO! It's a world centred on the four seasons...which I can only say YES PLEASE AND THANK YOU to.</b> Usually it's ice/fire/ear</span>
  <span id="freeText12855092661899959006" style="display:none">OH BREAK OUT THE CELEBRATORY POPSICLES! <b>THIS WAS ABSOLUTELY INCREDIBLE!</b> I feel the need to flail excessively because this was a super highly anticipated read for me. And it did. not. disappoint. YAY AND FINALLY. So let's make snow angels and hug icicles because I LOVE THIS BOOK.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427512468ra/14278950.gif" width="245" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, also, I have logical things to say. (Aren't you glad? I know you are, stop rolling your eyes.)<br><br><b>SO! It's a world centred on the four seasons...which I can only say YES PLEASE AND THANK YOU to.</b> Usually it's ice/fire/earth/water blah blah how many times I have a read that? But seasons?! YAY. It's not perfectly original, but it was fresh and delightful. I loved the cultures of all the seasons. I loved that winter was the abused mistreated race (because, to be cliche, they're usually the villains). So it was GORGEOUS. The world building was spectacular. Although there were a stack of info-dumps. And sometimes I got quite lost. Like the "whys" and "hows". (I was most wondering why ANYONE would ever team up and help Winter. Like what would the point of that be? Hm.. I'm sure it was explained I just didn't get that bit.)<br><br><b>And Meira?! SHE IS SO AWESOME.</b> She doesn't just crush cliches, so smacks them in the face. She's funny and a bit sarcastic. She's feisty and focused on being <i>her</i>, and not being compromised into someone else. She knows how to punch people, but it's not her sole focus in life. OH. And she's not above throwing a tantrum, which is <i>hilarious</i> and wonderful. I loved Meira. She's perfection of a heroine. <br><br>So then there's Mather, the future king, but you know...he and Meira are just ragged 16-year-olds in a group of 7 refugees (the ONLY 7 free people of the Winterians). Their relationship isn't <i>really</i> overly fleshed out. We know Meira has a crush on him, but she's nobody and he's future KING. So there's that. But I really struggled to care about Mather because he was so closed off. Even Meira said several times she could never tell what he was thinking and he was "unreadable". So, yeah, cool...but I didn't really ship them. <br><br><b>It has one of those OMG REALLY kind of plot twists...and I <i>loved it</i>.</b> Although, it was perfectly executed and written so so well BUT I DID KNOW IT WAS GOING TO HAPPEN. I don't know! Maybe it's because I'm a writer?! I was predicting it from like chapter 2 and I was so right. Which just makes me gleeful. And the twists have multiple layers, which is glorious.<br><br>ENDING SPOILERS!!! DO NOT OPEN OR ICICLES WILL EXPLODE YOUR BRAIN. ---&gt; <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ SO YEAH MEIRA IS THE QUEEN. HA! I totally sniffed that from chapter 2 when no one let her do anything. Why would they do that?! Unless it's blatant sexism, which I didn't think it <i>was</i> because there was so much emphasis on the queen of every country being the one who would wield the magic. As soon as I knew that I was like "Omg it's Meira." I didn't realise SHE was the conduit, though. There was no object, it was just her. That was awesome. Loved that. <br><br>Also, I know I'm bad but...I actually shipped Theron and Meira. I'M SORRY. I liked Mather but I didn't know him, and I like to know my ships. I like that Theron was interested in being himself, in poetry and art, and he would do what his family wanted, but that he actually had opinions/thoughts. Whereas Mather just did whatever he was told by Sir. (Sir is like, a jerk. But whatever. I guess he had reasons.)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Also I loved loved loved the descriptions.</b> SO MUCH AWESOME. Just with the Winterians having white hair and the Autumns being all brown and foresty and leafy. And omg, they had exclamations like "By the snow!" and it was just perfect and not cheesy at all. THE NAMES ARE ALSO PERFECT TOO. Names like "Mather" and "Noam" and "Abril" and "Jannuari".<br><br><b>My only real squinty moments are: </b> <br>a) it was super long and the middle particularly seemed to drag, <br>b) there were a few weird sexist remarks for a world that seemed SO feministic...why was the sexism there at all?! <br>c) the world was HUGE and sometimes I got really lost...like it took me a while to figure out that the 4 seasons weren't the only countries in the equation...I just wish the world had been a bit smaller, because there's lots to grasp.<br><br><b>It's pretty tough on the feels, just so you know.</b> This author does NOT spare her characters. EVERYONE gets hurt and battered and bad things happen to everyone and wowowow. I was constantly freaking out for everyone and that's <i>good writing</i>. Plus I just really loved the world.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427505110ra/14278235.gif" width="245" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>OKAY SO THIS BOOK IS GREAT NOW GO READ IT.</b> Swallow the icicles! Embrace the seasons! Sing Vivaldi if you must! Just go read this book. And if you have any doubts? JUST LET THEM GOOOOOO. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408293307ra/10832593.gif" width="500" height="247" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Oh COME ON. You knew that was coming. It's a book about WINTER. Of course I'm going to be spamming you with Frozen gifs. <br><br>HANG ON JUST WAIT! I have to tell you some of the hilarious quotes. <br><br><b>QUOTES OF NOTABLE AWESOME: </b><br><br><blockquote>"Congratulations, everyone," I announce as I open the door to Noam's study. "You've finally broken Meira, the crazy, orphaned soldier-grirl. She's snapped, all thanks to the mention of floral arrangements."</blockquote><br><br><blockquote> "I'm trying to learn more about magic," I start.<br>Theron gasps. "While reading a book called <i>Magic in Primoria? No!"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote> “So,” I start as we pull to the left in the hall, “you’re the king of Cordell’s son. How’s that?”<br>Theron chuckles. “Beneficial sometime, horrible others. You’re beautiful – how’s that?” </blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12855092661899959006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Clumsy Storyteller " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21493936-clumsy-storyteller"><img alt="Clumsy Storyteller " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542204051p2/21493936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1782614688?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clumsy Storyteller " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clumsy Storyteller " href="/user/show/21493936-clumsy-storyteller">Clumsy Storyteller </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy YA lovers</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782614688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17731843771625060336">“Fear is a seed that, once planted, never stops growing.” <br/><br/>EPIC. <br/><br/>Is the word that comes to mind to describe snow like ashes.<br/><br/>I was hesitant when I started reading it. I knew trouble were coming, 50 pages and they got the half locket? All they need to do is find the other half and get the magic back, easy task, right? I mean what could go wrong? <br/><br/>SPOILER: Everything went wrong.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393198072ra/8675345.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>The world building is phenomenal. We have 4 rhythms and 4 seasons. Ruled by 4 males and 4 females:<br/><br/>Seasons: <br/><br/>♥ Spring (Male):</span>
  <span id="freeText17731843771625060336" style="display:none">“Fear is a seed that, once planted, never stops growing.” <br><br>EPIC. <br><br>Is the word that comes to mind to describe snow like ashes.<br><br>I was hesitant when I started reading it. I knew trouble were coming, 50 pages and they got the half locket? All they need to do is find the other half and get the magic back, easy task, right? I mean what could go wrong? <br><br>SPOILER: Everything went wrong.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393198072ra/8675345.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The world building is phenomenal. We have 4 rhythms and 4 seasons. Ruled by 4 males and 4 females:<br><br>Seasons: <br><br>♥ Spring (Male): King Angra Manu who destroyed winter's kingdom sixteen years ago<br>♥ Winter (Female): Queen Hannah was killed by Angra. Her conduit was broken in half. and Magic disappeared.<br>♥ Autumn (Female) <br>♥ Summer (Male) <br><br>Rhythms:<br><br> ♥ Yakim (Female)<br> ♥ Ventralli (Male)<br> ♥ Paisly (Female) <br> ♥ Cordell (Male)<br><br>King Angra destryoed Winter and killed their queen and enslaved their people. Meira and 24 other winterians escaped, Only 10 of them remained alive. Meira's mission is to find Winter's conduit and restore magic to free her people. but there's one tiny, tiny problem...<br><br><b>“Even if we manage to get our female-blooded conduit put back together, how will we know if the magic works when our only heir is male?”</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489534768ra/22224250.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>“No matter what I want to do, no matter how well I lead or how hard I train, I won’t be able to force life into frozen fields, or cure plagues, or feed strength into soldiers like I would if I could use the conduit. The Winterians would probably rather have a cruel queen than a king with good intentions, because with a queen they at least have a chance that the magic can be used for them. It doesn’t matter what I would do with magic, because leaders are valued for the wrong things.”</b><br><br>Mather's Character was great. i didn't like the romance thou. Please Let Meira chose to be with theron. he's a much better match to her.<br><br><b>“I don’t need made-up strength. I’m strong enough on my own—me, Meira, no magic or conduit or anything.” </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446468185ra/16813216.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I. LOVE. HER.<br><br>Finally. a heroine that can save herself. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498835706ra/23165912.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315227312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5578390286135138906">And we have ANOTHER <b>DNF</b> 😂 Maybe I should stop trying to make progress on my backlist, eek<br/><br/><b>Yay</b><br/>1. Engaging writing style<br/>2. Strong heroine<br/>3. Royal politics<br/>4. Reclaiming a stolen kingdom<br/>5. Complex magic system<br/>6. Great character development<br/>7. Training montages<br/><br/><b>Nay</b><br/>1. Predictable plot<br/>2. Slavery trope<br/>3. Love triangle<br/>4. Lack of originality <br/>5. Gimmicky names (in terms of world building)<br/>6. Slow pacing<br/>7. Info dumps</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xTDIe7FhJZjaSk1y7y54AmX/sfRI30XhLSqaxc5V9vv/FqGpCj/s8H1h+RMY23Lds6BWPIZSy4Z2VNx0AxYEYQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MvOK49gWn6Nb9PmuOfJeON2JtrhC5uGeu466HBZ/fzII1eMxY0hWy/zfTc/OB1TnC9ZRcIxrb/ng8Pyt2zyNqA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer7647600000152696512">Sara Raasch has known she was destined for bookish things since the age of five, when her friends had a lemonade stand and she tagged along to sell her hand-drawn picture books too. Not much has changed since then — her friends still cock concerned eyebrows when she attempts to draw things and her enthusiasm for the written word still drives her to extreme measures. Her debut YA fantasy, SNOW LIKE</span>
  <span id="freeText7647600000152696512" style="display:none">Sara Raasch has known she was destined for bookish things since the age of five, when her friends had a lemonade stand and she tagged along to sell her hand-drawn picture books too. Not much has changed since then — her friends still cock concerned eyebrows when she attempts to draw things and her enthusiasm for the written word still drives her to extreme measures. Her debut YA fantasy, SNOW LIKE ASHES, the first in a trilogy, came out October 14, 2014 from Balzer + Bray. It does not feature her hand-drawn pictures.<br /></span>
